    var STYLE_ID = 'at-body-style';
    function getParent() {
    return doc.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
    }
    function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
        if (!parent) {
        return;
        }
        var style = doc.createElement('style');
        style.id = id;
        style.innerHTML = def;
        parent.appendChild(style);
    }
    function removeStyle(parent, id) {
        if (!parent) {
            return;
        }
        var style = doc.getElementById(id);
        if (!style) {
            return;
        }
        parent.removeChild(style);
    }
    addStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID, style);
    setTimeout(function() {
    removeStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID);

	function getCookie(cname) {
	 	var name = cname + "=";
  		var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
		var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
  		for(var i = 0; i <ca.length; i++) {
    			var c = ca[i];
    			while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
     				 c = c.substring(1);
    			}
    			if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
    				 return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
    			}
  		}
  		return "";
	}

	var referer = "";//sessionStorage.container;

function callMainSitePrismaNavHTML(){
    
    var referrer_domain = 'https://www.paloaltonetworks.com';
    sessionStorage.setItem("domain",referrer_domain);
    if(referer == 'Prisma'){
        //var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderPrisma.prismaRenderer.html';
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php?type=prisma&domain=en';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/prismasearch";
        }
    if(referer == 'CloudCortex'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php?type=cortexcloud&domain=en';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/cortexcloudsearch";	
    }
    if(referer == 'Cortex'){
        //var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderCortex.cortexRenderer.html';	
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php?type=cortex&domain=en';	
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/cortexsearch";	
    }
    if(referer == 'Sase'){
        //var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderSase.saseRenderer.html';
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php?type=sase&domain=en';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/sasesearch";
    }
    if(referer == 'Unit'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php?type=unit42&domain=en';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/content/pan/en_US/search/unit42search";
		    }
    if(referer == 'Ngfw'){
        //var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/ngfw-cdss-nav-renderer.php';
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php?type=ngfw&domain=en'; 
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/ngfwcdsssearch";
    }
    httpGet(menu_url,'menu_html');
    document.getElementById('main-nav-menu-cont').removeAttribute("style");
}
function addStyle(styles) {            
    /* Create style document */
    var css = document.createElement('style');
    css.type = 'text/css';

    if (css.styleSheet) 
        css.styleSheet.cssText = styles;
    else 
        css.appendChild(document.createTextNode(styles));

    /* Append style to the tag name */
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(css);
}
function httpGet(theUrl,req_type) {
    if (window.XMLHttpRequest) { // code for IE7+, Firefox, Chrome, Opera, Safari
        xmlhttp=new XMLHttpRequest();
    } else {// code for IE6, IE5
        xmlhttp=new ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
    }
    xmlhttp.onreadystatechange=function()
    {
        if (xmlhttp.readyState==4 && xmlhttp.status==200)
        {
            if(req_type == 'menu_html'){
            var nav_text = xmlhttp.responseText.replaceAll('https://static.cloud.coveo.com/searchui/v2.9159/js/CoveoJsSearch.Lazy.min.js', '');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll('src="/', 'src="'+maindomain_lang+'/');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll("'/content", "'"+maindomain_lang+"/content");
                        
            document.getElementById("PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC").innerHTML = nav_text.replaceAll('href="/', 'href="'+maindomain_lang+'/');

            var lozad_back = document.getElementsByClassName('lozad-background');
            Array.prototype.forEach.call(lozad_back, function(el) {
            // Do stuff here
            var el_back_img_path = el.getAttribute('data-background-image');
            var first_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'");
            var last_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'",first_pos+1);
            el_back_img_path = el_back_img_path.substring(first_pos+1,last_pos);
            el.setAttribute("data-background-image",main_site_url+el_back_img_path);
            });
            const observer_lozad = lozad('.lozad, .lozad-background'); // lazy loads elements with default selector as '.lozad'
            observer_lozad.observe();
            }
            if(req_type == 'head_inline_css'){
            addStyle(xmlhttp.responseText);
            }
        }
    }
    xmlhttp.open("GET", theUrl, true );
    xmlhttp.send();    
}

                <h2><a id="post-135181-_4lt92rr5muov"></a><strong>Executive Summary</strong></h2>
<p>This article lists selected threat actors tracked by Palo Alto Networks Unit 42, using our specific designators for these groups. We've organized them in alphabetical order of <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/unit-42-threat-group-naming-update/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">their assigned constellation</a>. The information presented here is a list of threat actors, along with key information like the category of threat actor, industries typically impacted and a summary of the overall threat. We intend this to be a centralized destination for readers to review the breadth of our research on these notable cyber threats. For more information on the attribution process, <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/unit-42-attribution-framework/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">read about Unit 42’s Attribution Framework</a>.</p>
<p>Palo Alto Networks customers are better protected from threat actors through the use of our products like our <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/next-generation-firewall" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Next-Generation Firewall</a> with <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/security-subscriptions" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cloud-Delivered Security Services</a> that include <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/advanced-wildfire" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced WildFire</a>, <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/advanced-dns-security" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced DNS Security</a>, <a href="https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/advanced-threat-prevention" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced Threat Prevention</a> and <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/advanced-url-filtering" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced URL Filtering</a>. Our customers are also better protected through our line of <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/cortex" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cortex</a> products and <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/sase" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Prisma SASE</a>.</p>
<p>If you think you might have been compromised or have an urgent matter, contact the <a href="https://start.paloaltonetworks.com/contact-unit42.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Unit 42 Incident Response team</a>.</p>

<td style="width: 35%;"><b>Related Unit 42 Topics</b></td>

<h2><a id="post-135181-_wven14kmgum2"></a><strong>Nation-State Threat Actor Groups </strong></h2>
<p>Unit 42 considers the following groups to have a motivation that is primarily state-backed rather than financial. There can also be some cybercrime motivation for threat groups in this category, but we believe their main motivation is in furthering the interest of their sponsoring nation.</p>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_3mk76bqcxp8"></a>Draco – Pakistan</h2>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136135 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/Draco-Pakistan-A-1920x900-1-786x368.png" alt="Pictorial representation of APT groups from Pakistan. The silhouette of a dragon and the Draco constellation inside an orange abstract planet. Abstract, stylized cosmic setting with vibrant blue and purple shapes, representing space and distant planetary bodies." width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/Draco-Pakistan-A-1920x900-1-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/Draco-Pakistan-A-1920x900-1-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/Draco-Pakistan-A-1920x900-1-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/Draco-Pakistan-A-1920x900-1-1536x720.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/Draco-Pakistan-A-1920x900-1.png 1920w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Draco, the dragon, is the constellation chosen for threat actor groups from Pakistan. These groups have been seen targeting India and other South Asian countries.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_76j4t5rhjd3r"></a>Mocking Draco</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_u8m8exwnds0j"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>G1008, sidecopy, unc2269, white dev 55</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_d6zb6bs65lo2"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Mocking Draco is a Pakistan-based threat actor that has been operating since at least 2019, mainly targeting South Asian countries and more specifically India and Afghanistan. Their malware’s common name, Sidecopy, comes from its infection chain that tries to mimic the malware SideWinder. This actor has reported similarities with Opaque Draco and is possibly a subdivision of this actor.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_crt0yfs94wjk"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Mocking Draco has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Government</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_gtzigwpcuib"></a>Opaque Draco</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_qwy9endfs0ce"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>APT36, C-Major, Cmajor, COPPER FIELDSTONE, Fast-Cargo, G0134, Green Halvidar, Havildar Team, Lapis, Mythic Leopard, ProjectM, Transparent Tribe</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_16iu1ru3yo1y"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Opaque Draco is a Pakistan-based threat group that has been active since 2013. They primarily target Indian governmental, military and educational sectors.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_6x5fith23hb6"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Opaque Draco has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Military</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_oj1yrcn0prnr"></a>Lynx – Belarus</h2>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136111 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-468772-135181-18.png" alt="" width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-468772-135181-18.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-468772-135181-18-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-468772-135181-18-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-468772-135181-18-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-468772-135181-18-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Belarusian threat groups are named for the constellation Lynx.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_bc1gttdd0t2t"></a>White Lynx</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_fjjq7opb2fif"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Ghostwriter, Storm-0257, UNC1151</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_o2vuxqdape5h"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>White Lynx is a nation-state threat actor assessed with high confidence to be linked with the Belarusian government. Their main focus is on countries neighboring Belarus, such as Ukraine, Lithuania, Latvia, Poland and Germany. Their targeting also includes Belarusian dissidents, media entities and journalists.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_45sxzd5rs80"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>White Lynx has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Construction</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Nonprofits</li>
<li>Pharma and Life Sciences</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>Real Estate</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_k9qe8684dfma"></a>Pisces – North Korea</h2>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136107 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-449925-135181-16.png" alt="" width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-449925-135181-16.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-449925-135181-16-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-449925-135181-16-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-449925-135181-16-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-449925-135181-16-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Threat actor groups attributed to North Korea are represented by the constellation Pisces. These groups have impacted many industries with a focus on cyberespionage and financial crime.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_c52dkzip4tuf"></a>Jumpy Pisces</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_1ivdobckktj5"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Andariel, Black Artemis, COVELLITE, Onyx Sleet, PLUTONIUM, Silent Chollima, Stonefly, UNC614, Lazarus, Lazarus Group</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_io5ul0ja1385"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Jumpy Pisces is a nation-state threat actor associated with the notorious Lazarus Group and the Democratic People’s Republic of Korea (DPRK). Jumpy Pisces is believed to be a subgroup of the Lazarus group that branched out around 2013. The group has demonstrated a high degree of adaptability, complexity and technical expertise in its operations, with a focus on cyber espionage, financial crime and ransomware attacks.</p>
<p>Jumpy Pisces primarily targets South Korean entities with a variety of attack vectors, including spear phishing, watering hole attacks and supply chain attacks. They have been observed exploiting vulnerabilities in various software, including asset management programs and known but unpatched public services, to distribute its malware. The group also abuses legitimate software and proxy and tunneling tools for its malicious activities.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_dmg8tedzwe10"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Jumpy Pisces has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Aerospace and Defense</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>IT Services</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Pharma and Life Sciences</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_3gkw3p8x5lku"></a>Slow Pisces</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_2mg67z2xmo2h"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Dark River, DEV-0954, Jade Sleet, Storm-0954, Trader Traitor, TraderTraitor, UNC4899, Lazarus, Lazarus Group</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_1p3xa6f1yf6z"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Slow Pisces is North Korea's nation state threat group under Reconnaissance General Bureau (RGB) of DPRK. It's believed to be a spin-off from the Lazarus group with focus on financial gathering and crypto industry targeting goals. Their primary task since 2020 is generating revenue for the DPRK regime and they do so by targeting organizations that handle large volumes of cryptocurrency. They have reportedly stolen in excess of $1 billion in 2023 alone.</p>
<p>Secondary to revenue generation, Slow Pisces has also compromised aerospace, defense and industrial organizations, likely with the aim of espionage to advance DPRK’s military capabilities.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_czshzcgdqnh7"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Slow Pisces has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Aerospace and Defense</li>
<li>Cryptocurrency Industry</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_fz7u6dt2bun9"></a>Serpens – Iran</h2>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136079 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-356998-135181-1.png" alt="" width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-356998-135181-1.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-356998-135181-1-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-356998-135181-1-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-356998-135181-1-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-356998-135181-1-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Iranian-attributed groups are named for the constellation Serpens, the snake. Our research on these groups highlights their targets and TTPs as they evolve.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_h4a6ereky174"></a>Academic Serpens</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_gkluj316qhai"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>COBALT DICKENS, DEV-0118, Mabna Institute, Silent Librarian, Yellow Nabu</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_3slp7hksfa3h"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Academic Serpens is a state-sponsored group active since at least 2013 that is attributed to Iran, which has traditionally focused on Middle Eastern targets and Nordic universities in the EU. Members of Academic Serpens are affiliated with the Iran-based Mabna Institute, which has conducted cyber intrusions at the behest of the government of Iran, specifically the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC). They have targeted research and proprietary data at universities, government agencies and private sector companies worldwide. There has been a notable decrease in activity from this group since the international COVID crisis in 2020.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_z2665xddsbgk"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Academic Serpens has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Government</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_1jt9nt9wga3m"></a>Agent Serpens</h3>
<h4>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Mint Sandstorm (Microsoft), Charming Kitten (Crowdstrike)</p>
<p>APT35, Ballistic Bobcat, Cobalt Illusion, Damselfly, Direfate, G0059, Greycatfish, Group 83, Iridium Group, ITG18, Magic Hound, Newscaster, Phosphorus, Saffron Rose, TA453, White Phosphorous, Yellow Garuda</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_u4irgz80ebgy"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Agent Serpens is a suspected nation-state threat actor the threat intelligence community attributes to Iran, with links to the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC). It has been active since at least 2015.</p>
<p>Agent Serpens is known for sophisticated social engineering (especially spear phishing), malware development and persistent, adaptive tactics. The group uses a diverse and evolving toolkit to facilitate all stages of their attacks, from initial access to command and control (C2). This includes custom-developed backdoors like SnailResin, SlugResin and Sponsor, which the threat actors designed to be used for gaining persistent access and data exfiltration.</p>
<p>The group's arsenal also features credential harvesting kits such as GCollection and DWP, which enable the theft of email user accounts. Agonizing Serpens abuses legitimate tools like PowerShell to deploy tools like AnvilEcho, TAMECAT and CharmPower that enable malicious activities within compromised environments.</p>
<p>The group's use of Android malware like PINEFLOWER demonstrates an interest in mobile surveillance, likely for monitoring targets and gathering intelligence. Additionally, Agent Serpens incorporates readily available open-source tools like Mimikatz, Chisel and Plink to augment their capabilities and support different phases of their operations.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_in3fs9d8fere"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Agent Serpens has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Automotive</li>
<li>Civil Engineering</li>
<li>Colleges And Universities</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>Higher Education</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Noncommercial</li>
<li>Research Organizations</li>
<li>Pharmaceutical and Life Sciences</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_23xtelqydolb"></a>Agonizing Serpens</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136081 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-368059-135181-2.jpeg" alt="" width="900" height="517" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-368059-135181-2.jpeg 1600w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-368059-135181-2-766x440.jpeg 766w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-368059-135181-2-1219x700.jpeg 1219w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-368059-135181-2-768x441.jpeg 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-368059-135181-2-1536x882.jpeg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<h4>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Pink Sandstrom (Microsoft), Spectral Kitten (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>Agrius, Americium, Black Shadow, Blackshadow, Cobalt Shadow, Darkrypt, UNC2428, Yellow Dev 21</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_cywe0d68the7"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/agonizing-serpens/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Agonizing Serpens</a> is a suspected nation-state threat actor attributed to Iran. This group has primarily disrupted Israeli organizations since 2020, and is linked to attacks throughout the Middle East. The group’s modus operandi involves strategically exfiltrating sensitive data before deploying destructive ransomware and wiper malware to disrupt systems and cover their tracks. This group has targeted organizations in the education, technology and financial sectors.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_hcwaaf4mp3aa"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Agonizing Serpens has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>IT Services</li>
<li>Nonclassifiable Establishments</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_cuofwfbjedpm"></a>Boggy Serpens</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_sc58byvcnh8x"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Mango Sandstorm (Microsoft), Static Kitten (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>Cobalt Ulster, Earth Vetala, G0069, Mercury, Muddywater, Seedworm, Temp.Zagros, Yellow Nix</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_rbp7cho88xln"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Active since at least 2017, Boggy Serpens is an Iranian, state-sponsored, cyberespionage group that US Cyber Command has attributed to Iran’s Ministry of Intelligence and Security (MOIS).</p>
<p>The group’s primary objective is cyberespionage aligned with Iranian government interests. This includes intelligence gathering, operational disruption and responding to regional conflicts, particularly those involving Israel.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_qzszf1ib898n"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Boggy Serpens has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_p4rb367v9bzo"></a>Devious Serpens</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_ga0xv8nyqbf0"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Cobalt Fireside, Curium, G1012, Imperial Kitten, Tortoiseshell, Yellow Liderc</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_x85i2gf11bb3"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Devious Serpens are an Iranian-based threat actor known for using social engineering tactics as well as malware that communicates via IMAP. Their attacks use watering hole attacks as well as their own controlled sites meant to impersonate employment opportunities that might interest their victims.</p>
<p>The malware that they have built often uses IMAP with specific email addresses for command and control (C2). With such tools, communication typically occurs via specific folders and message protocols on the C2 email address.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_7q3m8hv0atng"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Devious Serpens has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Aerospace and Defense</li>
<li>Information Technology Services</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_y3gspdywzn5t"></a>Evasive Serpens</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_lwa4fc2dppps"></a><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136083 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-371133-135181-3.jpeg" alt="" width="900" height="551" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-371133-135181-3.jpeg 1505w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-371133-135181-3-718x440.jpeg 718w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-371133-135181-3-1143x700.jpeg 1143w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-371133-135181-3-768x470.jpeg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></h4>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_6x7hl0ln6mc1"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Alibaba, APT34, Chrysene, Cobalt Gypsy, Crambus, Europium, G0049, Group 41, Hazel Sandstorm, Helix Kitten, IRN2, OilRig, Powbat, TEMP.Akapav, Twisted Kitten, Yossi</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_jmc7fsp87peh"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Evasive Serpens is a threat group Unit 42 discovered in May 2016. They are a nation-state threat group attributed to Iran. This threat group is extremely persistent and relies heavily on spear phishing as their initial attack vector. However, they have also been associated with other more complex attacks such as credential harvesting campaigns and DNS hijacking.</p>
<p>In their spear phishing attacks, Evasive Serpens preferred macro-enabled Microsoft Office (Word and Excel) documents to install their custom payloads that came as portable executables (PE), PowerShell and VBScripts. The group’s custom payloads frequently used DNS tunneling as a C2 channel.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_b68fxw9eu4a0"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Evasive Serpens has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chemical Manufacturing</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_pm5zobhuwkgz"></a>Taurus – China</h2>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136085 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-374538-135181-4.png" alt="" width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-374538-135181-4.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-374538-135181-4-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-374538-135181-4-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-374538-135181-4-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-374538-135181-4-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Chinese threat actor groups take their name from the constellation Taurus – the bull. Due to the long history and multiplicity of Chinese APTs, there is a lot to be discovered about these groups in our research archives.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_tqzx2rpfkie5"></a>Alloy Taurus</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136087 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-381051-135181-5.jpeg" alt="" width="900" height="551" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-381051-135181-5.jpeg 1505w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-381051-135181-5-718x440.jpeg 718w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-381051-135181-5-1143x700.jpeg 1143w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-381051-135181-5-768x470.jpeg 768w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_9p1ytiqf6d6a"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Granite Typhoon (Microsoft), Phantom Panda (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>G0093, Gallium, Operation Soft Cell, Othorene, Red Dev 4</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_nh56a0pps2ek"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/alloy-taurus/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Alloy Taurus</a> has been active since at least 2012 and is a suspected nation-state threat actor group attributed to China.</p>
<p>The group is known for its long-term cyberespionage campaigns, primarily targeting telecommunications companies, government entities and financial institutions across Southeast Asia, Europe and Africa. Their operations are characterized by multi-wave intrusions aimed at establishing persistent footholds within compromised networks.</p>
<p>Alloy Taurus gains initial access by exploiting vulnerabilities in internet-facing applications.</p>
<p>Alloy Taurus employs a range of custom and modified malware for multiple operating systems to enhance their espionage capabilities, move laterally and evade detection. This includes backdoors, web shells, credential harvesting tools as well as legitimate applications, such as VPN and remote management tools.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_bwybb07fva0m"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Alloy Taurus has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_uqlllgl5mgwi"></a>Charging Taurus</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_sy1288gigdf9"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Circle Typhoon, DEV-0322, TGR-STA-0027, Tilted Temple</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_gb7bxoorigza"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Charging Taurus is a state-sponsored cyberespionage group attributed to China, active since 2021. The group's goal is to steal intellectual property aligned with China's national interests. The group is capable of exploiting undisclosed zero-day vulnerabilities. The group has a possible tie to <a href="#post-135181-_q3xis2d3s34f">Insidious Taurus</a>.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_j2r8ri5k0e66"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_4uxrab1zqwvx"></a>Dicing Taurus</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_vmkbg85kxhmi"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Jackpot Panda</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_civxc5y573fo"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Dicing Taurus is a state-sponsored group attributed to China. They focus on the illegal online gambling sector in Southeast Asia, particularly emphasizing data collection for monitoring and countering related activities in China. The i-Soon leak in February 2024 revealed that i-Soon was likely involved in Dicing Taurus's operations, along with the Ministry of Public Security of China.</p>
<p>The group is also responsible for distributing a trojanized installer for CloudChat, a chat application popular with Chinese-speaking illegal gambling communities in mainland China. The trojanized installer served from CloudChat’s website contained the first stage of a multi-step process.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_rz28nn7a452n"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Dicing Taurus has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Online Gambling</li>
<li>Software and Technology</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_tqbqkssp1nvu"></a>Digging Taurus</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_uvzl68oyh2o2"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>BRONZE HIGHLAND, Daggerfly, Evasive Panda, StormBamboo</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_1j1dg08gql0o"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Digging Taurus is a suspected nation-state threat group attributed to China, which has been active since at least 2012. The group targets organizations from around the world, including those in Taiwan, Hong Kong, Mainland China, India and Africa. Their activities, including intelligence collection, align with Chinese interests. This group has targeted organizations with advanced malware frameworks like MgBot and CloudScout. They strategically use different initial access vectors, including supply-chain attacks and DNS poisoning.</p>

<p>Digging Taurus has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>

<li>Executive Offices</li>
<li>General Government Administration</li>
<li>Local Government</li>
<li>Nonprofit</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
</ul>

<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136089 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-384223-135181-6.jpeg" alt="" width="900" height="517" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-384223-135181-6.jpeg 1600w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-384223-135181-6-766x440.jpeg 766w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-384223-135181-6-1219x700.jpeg 1219w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-384223-135181-6-768x441.jpeg 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-384223-135181-6-1536x882.jpeg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_c7zj4c8ogv23"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>BRONZE SILHOUETTE, DEV-0391, UNC3236, Vanguard Panda, Volt Typhoon, Voltzite, G1017</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_8pjib2wwlb00"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/insidious-taurus/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Insidious Taurus</a> is a Chinese state-sponsored actor typically focusing on espionage and information gathering, active since 2021. Insidious Taurus evades detection by using various living-off-the-land (LotL) techniques, using in-built system tools to perform their objectives and blend in with regular system noise.</p>
<p>The actor leverages compromised small office/home office (SOHO) network devices as intermediate infrastructure to further obscure their activity. Insidious Taurus exploits vulnerabilities in internet-facing devices and systems as an initial access vector.</p>

<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
<li>Utilities</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_x3qts2x8kbfg"></a>Jumper Taurus</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_w9hivzujn3a3"></a>Also Known As</h4>

<h4><a id="post-135181-_7mwrp1fc8uf9"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Jumper Taurus is a state-sponsored cyberespionage group believed to be linked to the Chinese government. Active since at least 2013, the group has consistently demonstrated advanced tactics, techniques and procedures (TTPs), supporting China's strategic objectives in sensitive research or holding strategic geopolitical relationships.</p>
<p>The group's operations use phishing emails and exploit web server vulnerabilities for initial access. The group has shown a particular interest in maritime-related targets, those associated with China's naval modernization efforts and the Belt and Road Initiative.</p>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_wfgy859vfe4q"></a>Stately Taurus</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_51pstjp05h3l"></a><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136093 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-390072-135181-8.jpeg" alt="" width="900" height="517" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-390072-135181-8.jpeg 1600w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-390072-135181-8-766x440.jpeg 766w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-390072-135181-8-1219x700.jpeg 1219w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-390072-135181-8-768x441.jpeg 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-390072-135181-8-1536x882.jpeg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></h4>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_i435lmvf2bmb"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Twill Typhoon (Microsoft), Mustang Panda (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>Bronze Fillmore, BRONZE PRESIDENT, DEV-0117, Earth Preta, G0129, HoneyMyte, Luminous Moth, PKPLUG, Red Lich, RedDelta, TA416, Tantalum, TEMP.Hex</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_hsxqzajcgvj1"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/stately-taurus/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Stately Taurus</a> is a nation-state threat actor attributed to China. The group has been active since at least 2012. Their campaigns are designed to gather sensitive information and exert political influence, aligning with Chinese state interests. This includes monitoring and influencing political developments in regions of strategic importance, such as the South China Sea and areas involved in the global 5G rollout.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_iqvy6872mhe"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Stately Taurus has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>National Security</li>
<li>Professional and Legal services</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_sdi60y7bb18"></a>Ursa – Russia</h2>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136095 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-394029-135181-9.png" alt="Pictorial representation of Russian threat actor groups. <p>Russian threat groups tracked by Unit 42 are named for the Ursa constellation. We report on these groups regularly and have a significant archive of material.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_mvwvekj93ho9"></a>Cloaked Ursa</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136097 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-409825-135181-10.jpeg" alt="Pictorial representation of APT Cloaked Ursa. <h4><a id="post-135181-_bffdxmvz9aw6"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Midnight Blizzard (Microsoft), Cozy Bear (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>APT29, Backswimmer, Blue Kitsune, Blue Nova, Cozy, CozyDuke, Dark Halo, DEV-0473, Dukes, Eurostrike, G0016, Group 100, Hagensia, Iron Hemlock, Iron Ritual, Nobelium, Noblebaron, Office Monkeys, Office Space, Solarstorm, TAG-11, The Dukes, UAC-0029, UNC2452, UNC3524, YTTRIUM</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_smfaksx8tx2"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/cloaked-ursa/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cloaked Ursa</a> is a nation-state threat actor attributed to Russia's Foreign Intelligence Service (SVR) that has been active since at least 2008. This group targets government, diplomatic, and critical infrastructure entities worldwide across regions such as North America, Europe, and countries opposing Russian geopolitical objectives. Cloaked Ursa's primary focus is intelligence gathering and data exfiltration to support Russian foreign policy goals, gain strategic advantage in geopolitical conflicts, and monitor and disrupt the activities of perceived adversaries.</p>

<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
</ul>

<h4><a id="post-135181-_p183v1ldppl4"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/fighting-ursa/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Fighting Ursa</a> is a nation-state threat group attributed to Russia’s General Staff Main Intelligence Directorate (GRU), 85th special Service Centre (GTsSS) military intelligence Unit 26165. They are well known for their focus on targets of Russian interest, especially those of military interest. They are known as one of the two Russian groups that compromised the Democratic National Committee (DNC) and Democratic Congressional Campaign Committee (DCCC) during the 2016 election cycle.</p>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_egjcna9cmdqh"></a>Mythic Ursa</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_d42s034i8wgi"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Blue Callisto, Callisto, Callisto Group, COLDRIVER, Dancing Salome, Grey Pro, IRON FRONTIER, Reuse Team, SEABORGIUM, Star Blizzard</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_i8znijlj4qc5"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Mythic Ursa is a Russian group linked to Russia’s “Centre 18” Federal Security Service (FSB) division, focused on credential harvesting from high-profile individuals. This group often uses fake accounts to establish rapport with their targets and eventually sends a phishing link to gather credentials. This group was last observed using custom malware in November 2022.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_j9leasc8r38m"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>

<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
</ul>

<h4><a id="post-135181-_7mydxgvnijds"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/trident-ursa/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Trident Ursa</a> is a nation-state threat group that has been active since at least 2013. This group has targeted individuals likely related to the Ukrainian government and military and is likely the actor behind the 2015 Operation Armageddon that delivered remote access tools, such as UltraVNC and Remote Manipulator System (RMS). The group previously used commodity tools but began using custom-developed tools in 2016.</p>

</ul>
<h2><a id="post-135181-_yay5kgscoqyi"></a><strong>Cybercrime Threat Actor Groups</strong></h2>
<p>Unit 42 considers the following groups to have a motivation that is primarily financial rather than political. There can be some political motivation for threat groups in this category, but we consider their main motivation to be perpetrating cybercrime. This category is split into two groups: cybercrime in general, and then ransomware.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_kfgx4ats00y0"></a>Libra – Cybercrime</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136115 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-483104-135181-20.png" alt="" width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-483104-135181-20.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-483104-135181-20-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-483104-135181-20-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-483104-135181-20-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-483104-135181-20-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Cybercrime is represented by the constellation Libra – a fitting choice, using the imagery of scales of justice.</p>
<h3>Bling Libra</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-148809 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/03-2-Bling-Libra-1920x900-1-786x368.png" alt="Pictorial representation of APT Bling Libra. The silhouette of a set of scales and the Libra constellation inside an orange abstract planet. Abstract, stylized cosmic setting with vibrant blue and purple shapes, representing space and distant planetary bodies." width="786" height="368" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/03-2-Bling-Libra-1920x900-1-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/03-2-Bling-Libra-1920x900-1-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/03-2-Bling-Libra-1920x900-1-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/03-2-Bling-Libra-1920x900-1-1536x720.png 1536w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/03-2-Bling-Libra-1920x900-1.png 1920w" sizes="(max-width: 786px) 100vw, 786px" /></p>
<h4>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Shiny Hunters, ShinyCorp, ShinyHunters, UNC5537</p>
<h4>Summary</h4>
<p>Bling Libra is an extortionist group and data broker active since at least 2020. Initially operating on RaidForums, a key member now holds an administrative role on BreachForums.</p>
<p>The group publishes stolen data, particularly after failed extortion attempts, to bolster its reputation. Bling Libra targets industries worldwide, including telecommunications, financial services, entertainment and high technology, across the U.S., Europe, Asia, the Middle East and Latin America.</p>
<p>The group gains access through stolen credentials obtained via infostealer malware and phishing campaigns. Its tactics include exploiting unsecured cloud storage, weak security configurations, and using custom tools like FROSTBITE along with publicly available tools.</p>
<h4>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Bling Libra has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Real Estate</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_st9zfqylkm36"></a>Muddled Libra</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136117 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-491765-135181-21.jpeg" alt="" width="900" height="517" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-491765-135181-21.jpeg 1600w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-491765-135181-21-766x440.jpeg 766w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-491765-135181-21-1219x700.jpeg 1219w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-491765-135181-21-768x441.jpeg 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-491765-135181-21-1536x882.jpeg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_kymqh961r2b9"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Octo Tempest (Microsoft), Scattered Spider (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>G1015, Roasted 0ktapus, Scatter Swine, Star Fraud, UNC3944</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_fd5t6mfes4kb"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/muddled-libra/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Muddled Libra</a> is a financially motivated cyberthreat group active since at least May 2022.</p>
<p>The group is composed of English-speaking members, some as young as 16. The group initially engaged in SIM swapping and credential harvesting, primarily targeting individuals for cryptocurrency theft. They have since evolved their operations to include data theft and ransomware deployment, aiming to extort large organizations for financial gain. Primarily targeting U.S.-based companies, Muddled Libra has expanded its focus from telecommunications and business process outsourcing (BPO) sectors to a diverse range of industries such as retail, hospitality, gaming, manufacturing and financial services.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_3n9leq2rqg3k"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Muddled Libra has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_ej9k4gb0ryb"></a>Scorpius – Ransomware</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-136113 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-477669-135181-19.png" alt="" width="900" height="422" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-477669-135181-19.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-477669-135181-19-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-477669-135181-19-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-477669-135181-19-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/word-image-477669-135181-19-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /></p>
<p>Ransomware groups get their naming convention from the constellation Scorpius, and are a frequent target of our research.</p>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_6b87k8xk6fc4"></a>Ambitious Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_it8mof9m7tki"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>ALPHV, BlackCat, blackcat_raas</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_if7f2rdns3b"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/ambitious-scorpius/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Ambitious Scorpius</a> is a RaaS group that uses multi-extortion, distributing BlackCat ransomware. The ransomware family was first observed in November 2021. The group is suspected to be of Russian origin and is a possible successor of DarkSide and BlackMatter. The group solicits for affiliates in known cybercrime forums, offering to allow them to keep 80-90% of the ransom payment.</p>
<p>A significant disruption by joint law enforcement in December 2023 appears to have dealt the group a significant blow. Despite actively listing new victims through February 2024, about 40% of the victims were smaller businesses rather than the high value targets usually seen.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_ggqaa38xc8ns"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Ambitious Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Aerospace and Defense</li>
<li>Agriculture</li>
<li>Construction</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Mining</li>
<li>Nonprofits</li>
<li>Pharma and Life Sciences</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>Real Estate</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_oau4a8hwv233"></a>Bashful Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_hyd66yn78hlv"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Nokoyawa</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_l08vickpuzoh"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Bashful Scorpius ransomware group was first observed in February 2022, distributing Nokoyawa ransomware, which is potentially an evolution of Nemty and Karma ransomware. Bashful Scorpius uses a multi-extortion strategy, in which attackers demand payment both for a decryptor to restore access to encrypted files and for not disclosing stolen data.</p>
<p>This group distributes their ransomware payloads through various means, including third-party frameworks such as Cobalt Strike and phishing emails. The creators of Nokoyawa ransomware have repurposed functions from the leaked Babuk ransomware source code.</p>
<p>Ransomware operators using Nokoyawa ransomware wield a command set that allows them to exercise precise control over the execution and ultimate outcome of the infection. This further increases the threat’s effectiveness and potential damage.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_sspszciojqs9"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Bashful Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Agriculture</li>
<li>Construction</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Finance</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Nonprofits</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_yihojoju9dok"></a>Bitter Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_dgtctf8o2nqb"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>BianLian, bianlian_group</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_t68q7smu86yj"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Initially discovered in July 2022, <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/bitter-scorpius/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Bitter Scorpius</a> is a ransomware group that uses double-extortion (T1486, T1657). The group is known for being highly adaptable and quickly leverages newly disclosed vulnerabilities. They have been among the top ten most active ransomware groups since 2023.</p>
<p>Bitter Scorpius distributes the BianLian ransomware, which is written in the Go programming language. The group gains initial access by exploiting external-facing remote services (T1190, T1133) and using custom remote access malware to maintain persistence.</p>
<p>According to previous research, the threat actors appear technically sophisticated in compromising targeted networks but are likely inexperienced overall based on the following behaviors observed during investigations:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mistakenly sends data from one victim to another</li>
<li>Possesses a relatively stable backdoor toolkit but an encryption tool that remains in active development, including an evolving ransom note</li>
<li>Maintains unreliable infrastructure, as stated through the group's admission on their Onion site</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_k4k15edpyxwn"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_tuitqpq8wqvn"></a>Blustering Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_juj6xcwfo7gi"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Stormous</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_soaavx9l70jd"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Blustering Scorpius is an Arabic-speaking cybercrime group that first appeared in 2021. They gained fame by exploiting tensions in the Russia-Ukraine war and targeting Western entities in 2022. They initially sought to specifically target entities in the U.S. but quickly began targeting entities based on global political tensions. While the group has claimed numerous attacks, they have also been accused of posting fake data or claiming attacks perpetrated by other groups.</p>
<p>Blustering Scorpius gains initial access via phishing, vulnerability exploits, remote data protocol (RDP), credential abuse and malvertising. They use X (Twitter) and Telegram to advertise their exploits and to reach their followers and affiliates. The group also uses social engineering to exploit emotions surrounding geopolitical tensions.</p>
<p>Blustering Scorpius began joint operations with GhostSec on July 13, 2023, which they announced via GhostSec’s Telegram channel. The two groups have gone on to jointly attack multiple entities in various countries and industries.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_ekbm5240zjfu"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Blustering Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_ow29ue96ir8j"></a>Chubby Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_ttzzmb2jvzk8"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Cl0p, CL0P</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_5dqsxvtjd87"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>The <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/chubby-scorpius/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Chubby Scorpius</a> group, first observed <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/clop-ransomware/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">in February 2019</a>, is a financially motivated ransomware group known for its sophisticated operations and large-scale attacks using the Cl0P ransomware. They operate under a ransomware-as-a-service (RaaS) model, meaning they develop and maintain the ransomware while affiliates carry out the attacks.</p>
<p>In June 2021, <a href="https://www.interpol.int/en/News-and-Events/News/2021/INTERPOL-led-operation-takes-down-prolific-cybercrime-ring" target="_blank" rel="noopener">six suspected members of the Cl0p ransomware gang were arrested</a> in Ukraine during a series of raids conducted in and around Kyiv. Ukrainian law enforcement, working with investigators from South Korea and the United States, searched 21 homes and seized various devices including computers, smartphones and servers. They also confiscated approximately $184,000 USD in what is believed to be ransom payments.</p>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_pjexkwz5bli8"></a>Dapper Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_3wugkskqptz3"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>BlackSuit</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_t3b2i532nyzd"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Dapper Scorpius is a ransomware group that emerged in early May 2023, distributing BlackSuit ransomware, impacting a broad range of organizations globally. This group is suspected to be the Ignoble Scorpius ransomware group (aka Royal Ransomware) rebranded.</p>
<p>Unlike many ransomware operations that use a RaaS model, Dapper Scorpius operates as a private group without affiliates, most likely composed of ex-Conti and ex-Ignoble Scorpius members. Dapper Scorpius employs a multifaceted distribution strategy that includes phishing campaigns, malicious email attachments, SEO poisoning and using loaders like GootLoader for deploying their ransomware payload.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_n8mhxxp9xlzi"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_jn4trlny2pqi"></a>Dark Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_qn8250am7lhm"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Storm-1811 (Microsoft), Curly Spider (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>Black Basta, Black_Basta, BlackBasta, Cardina, UNC4393</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_q7atc588h4yr"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/dark-scorpius/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Dark Scorpius</a> is a financially motivated ransomware-as-a-service (RaaS) group, with suspected ties to the defunct Conti group. These two groups use similar tactics, techniques, procedures (TTPs) and infrastructure.</p>
<p>Dark Scorpius operations involve double extortion, encrypting data (T1486) and threatening public disclosure of sensitive information to coerce ransom payments (T1657). First observed in April 2022, they target critical infrastructure and high-profile organizations globally, causing significant disruptions and financial losses.</p>
<p>While Dark Scorpius has impacted organizations globally, their reported compromises skewed more toward developed countries such as the U.S., UK, Germany and Canada. While organizations in developed countries are most frequently targeted due to their potential for high-value payouts, this threat actor maintains an opportunistic approach, suggesting they will target any vulnerable organization if the opportunity for profit arises. The group avoids operations within the Commonwealth of Independent States, a common behavior observed in Russia-based groups.</p>
<p>As a RaaS group, Dark Scorpius has affiliates that leverage a wide set of TTPs to achieve their objectives. As such, what we capture in this report may differ from the activities they employ in future attacks.</p>
<p>The group exclusively uses the Black Basta ransomware for data encryption (T1486) after exfiltrating files with tools such as RClone (S1040, T1048, T1567).</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_mcveabo8t5lp"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_hkav8lltuxgd"></a>Fiddling Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_bntshuja1rlq"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Play, PlayCrypt</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_xtv9qw7iz0n"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Fiddling Scorpius is a sophisticated cybercriminal organization that emerged in June 2022. This group is notorious for its double-extortion tactics, where they exfiltrate sensitive data before encrypting systems and demanding ransom payments to prevent data leaks.</p>
<p>The tooling employed by Fiddling Scorpius includes a mix of custom and publicly available tools for command and control (C2), lateral movement, credential dumping, and data exfiltration. The primary impact of their attacks is data encryption with a <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">.play</span> extension, causing significant operational disruptions.</p>

<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-148820 size-full lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-26-Fiery-Scorpius-1920x900-1.jpg" alt="Pictorial representation of APT Fiery Scorpius. <h3>Flighty Scorpius</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-148831 size-full lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-15-Flighty-Scorpius-1920x900-1.jpg" alt="Pictorial representation of APT Flighty Scorpius. The silhouette of a scorpion and the Scorpius constellation inside an orange abstract planet. Abstract, stylized cosmic setting with vibrant blue and purple shapes, representing space and distant planetary bodies." width="1920" height="900" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-15-Flighty-Scorpius-1920x900-1.jpg 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-15-Flighty-Scorpius-1920x900-1-786x368.jpg 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-15-Flighty-Scorpius-1920x900-1-1493x700.jpg 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-15-Flighty-Scorpius-1920x900-1-768x360.jpg 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-15-Flighty-Scorpius-1920x900-1-1536x720.jpg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px" /></p>
<h4>Also Known As</h4>
<p>ABCD, LockBit, LockBit 2.0, LockBit 3.0, LockBit Black, Lockbit_RaaS</p>
<h4>Summary</h4>
<p>Flighty Scorpius is a ransomware as a service (RaaS) group, first observed in September 2019. They were initially known for deploying ABCD ransomware, which was so named due to its characteristic .<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">abcd</span> file extension used during attacks. They later rebranded as LockBit when they became a RaaS operation.</p>
<p>Flighty Scorpius' operational model is distinguished by its affiliate program, which they aggressively marketed on underground forums. The group has innovated in affiliate relations, offering direct ransom payments to affiliates before taking its cut, a practice that contrasts with the norm and incentivizes potential partners.</p>
<p>Over the years, Flighty Scorpius has developed and released multiple LockBit ransomware variants. Each variant signifies an evolution in the group's technical capabilities, from faster encryption speeds to more sophisticated extortion techniques. This evolution is mostly as a result of their acquiring different ransomware source code from competitors.</p>
<p>The group suffered a major disruption with Operation Cronos in February 2024, which led to law enforcement seizing infrastructure and public-facing websites crucial to LockBit's operations. They also exposed Russian nationals as members of the group, including its administrator.</p>
<p>Despite these law enforcement disruptions Flighty Scorpius has resumed operations, including the potential release of a new ransomware variant.</p>

<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Mining</li>

<li>Real Estate</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>

<h3>Fluttering Scorpius</h3>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-148842 size-full lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-8-Fluttering-Scorpius-1920x900-1.png" alt="Pictorial representation of APT Fluttering Scorpius. The silhouette of a scorpion and the Scorpius constellation inside an orange abstract planet. Abstract, stylized cosmic setting with vibrant blue and purple shapes, representing space and distant planetary bodies." width="1920" height="900" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-8-Fluttering-Scorpius-1920x900-1.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-8-Fluttering-Scorpius-1920x900-1-786x368.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-8-Fluttering-Scorpius-1920x900-1-1493x700.png 1493w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-8-Fluttering-Scorpius-1920x900-1-768x360.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/06/07-8-Fluttering-Scorpius-1920x900-1-1536x720.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px" /></p>
<h4>Also Known As</h4>
<p>FOG</p>
<h4>Summary</h4>
<p>Fluttering Scorpius, the group that distributes FOG ransomware, emerged as a significant threat actor in the ransomware landscape when first observed in April 2024. This group is notorious for exploiting vulnerabilities in widely used software to gain unauthorized access to systems.</p>
<p>The group employs various techniques, like using stolen credentials and unpatched vulnerabilities to infiltrate networks. Fluttering Scorpius has shared infrastructure with the Akira ransomware group, which suggests possible collaboration between these groups.</p>
<p>Fluttering Scorpius' operations are marked by rapid encryption attacks and strategically using living-off-the-land binaries (LOLBins) to evade detection.</p>
<p>The group focuses on targeting backup and disaster recovery solutions to maximize the impact of their attacks. The group often uses compromised VPN credentials to get a foothold in the victim's environment. These threat actors accomplish lateral movement using pass-the-hash attacks on administrator accounts to establish RDP connections targeting Hyper-V running on Windows servers. Fluttering Scorpius also uses credential stuffing to take over high-value accounts.</p>

<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Nonprofits</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_tyo3xil0xez1"></a>Howling Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_mtiqj54qupki"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Storm-1567 (Microsoft), Punk Spider (CrowdStrike)</p>
<p>Akira</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_bdkqu9d5h2vj"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Howling Scorpius is a financially motivated ransomware-as-a-service (RaaS) operation observed since early 2023. It employs double extortion tactics, exfiltrating sensitive data before typically encrypting systems.</p>
<p>The group targets organizations globally, with a focus on North America, the UK, Australia and Europe. It impacts various sectors, including manufacturing, professional services, education, critical infrastructure and retail.</p>
<p>Howling Scorpius targets Windows and Linux/ESXi systems with evolving ransomware variants. It uses various tactics, including exploiting vulnerabilities and credential theft, to exfiltrate data.</p>
<p>Dwell times range from less than 24 hours to a month, likely reflecting varying affiliate capabilities. While Howling Scorpius primarily uses double extortion, threatening to publish stolen data if ransom demands are unmet, it has also engaged in extortion-only attacks. In cases we observed during Fall 2023, the group exfiltrated data for payment extortion without deploying ransomware.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_lhhhnnnuqbht"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Howling Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>

<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Health Insurance Providers</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Healthcare</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">High Technology</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Hospitality</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Hospitality Industry</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Industrial Products And Services Industry</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Information Technology (IT) or Technology Consulting Industry</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Insurance</span></li>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_88qmqns06x8v"></a>Ignoble Scorpius</h3>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_akmfezbo2bbo"></a>Also Known As</h3>
<p>Black Suit, BlackSuit, Dapper Scorpius, Roy, Royal, Royal_Group, Zeon</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_fl3fq5aoclt7"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/ignoble-scorpius/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Ignoble Scorpius</a> is a cybercriminal organization specializing in ransomware attacks. First emerging in September 2022 as the Royal ransomware group, it rebranded as BlackSuit around May 2023.</p>
<p>This group comprises experienced members possibly linked to the defunct Conti group. It has developed custom ransomware payloads, notably introducing the BlackSuit ransomware as a successor to the earlier Royal ransomware. BlackSuit retained over 90% of Royal's codebase.</p>
<p>The group's ransomware targets Windows and Linux systems, including ESXi servers and employs strong encryption algorithms to render data inaccessible.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_fkjrsp9lyqv0"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Ignoble Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>

<h3><a id="post-135181-_yp7g8hvawfoi"></a>Invisible Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_owla59q12t07"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Cloak</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_3xxk4ha72rf6"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Invisible Scorpius is a ransomware group targeting small to medium-sized businesses and using initial access brokers (IABs) for initial access. First seen at the end of 2022, the group is believed to be connected to the Stale Scorpius ransomware group after threat actors posted victim information from Stale Scorpius to Invisible Scorpius' leak site.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_t64nuafgvmw"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Invisible Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_9eimw0pj38ls"></a>Mushy Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_sip4ozp7hyxq"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Karakurt, Karakurt Lair, Karakurt Team</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_oaf2zmd4gmu2"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Mushy Scorpius is the group behind Karakurt ransomware, known for focusing on extortion. It has links to the Conti RaaS group. First emerging in 2021, Mushy Scorpius steals intellectual property and demands ransom from victims without encrypting their data, leveraging threats to auction off the sensitive data or release it to the public.</p>
<p>As part of their extortion efforts, they provide victims with screenshots or copies of stolen file directories as evidence of the data theft. They aggressively contact victims' employees, business partners and clients with harassing emails and phone calls. They also leverage stolen data like social security numbers, payment accounts, private emails and other sensitive business information to exert pressure.</p>
<p>Upon receiving ransom payments, Mushy Scorpius has occasionally provided victims with proof that they deleted the stolen files, along with a brief explanation of how they initially breached the victim's defenses. This underlines the group’s focus on financial gain but also that they seek a level of engagement from their victims toward meeting their demands.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_dmtehyynfcbe"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Mushy Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Agriculture</li>
<li>Construction</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>High Technology</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Media and Entertainment</li>
<li>Nonprofits</li>
<li>Pharma and Life Sciences</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>Real Estate</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Telecommunications</li>
<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_4fp8x84ypcsp"></a>Pilfering Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_fxur23gu85o2"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>Robinhood</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_clyyjonvvi8n"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Pilfering Scorpius ransomware group gained attention by attacking a number of local and state government entities starting in April 2019. This threat group often gains initial access by phishing, malicious websites and malicious file sharing or downloads.</p>
<p>Once their ransomware has gained access, it obtains persistence by using RDP to spread throughout the victim network. Initial reporting revealed that humans were largely responsible for operating these attacks, as opposed to them being run by automated processes.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_8adnnccur51v"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Pilfering Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>

<li>Utilities and Energy</li>
<li>Transportation and Logistics</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Nonprofits</li>
<li>Insurance</li>
<li>Healthcare</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Federal Government</li>
<li>State and Local Government</li>
<li>Real Estate</li>
<li>Construction</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Agriculture</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_8bbk3jl9h014"></a>Powerful Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_s9kz8c43nls7"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>BlackByte</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_z8vrbxuggdiq"></a>Summary</h4>
<p><a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/powerful-scorpius/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Powerful Scorpius</a> is a RaaS group operating since July 2021, distributing BlackByte ransomware. This group’s operational tactics includes exploiting vulnerabilities such as the ProxyShell vulnerability in Microsoft Exchange Servers, using tools like Cobalt Strike, and avoiding detection through obfuscation and anti-debugging techniques.</p>
<p>Their malware checks system languages and exits if it finds Russian or certain Eastern European languages, presumably to avoid impacting systems in those regions. The group uses multi-extortion techniques in their campaigns.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_43qb65vprj3f"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Powerful Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Food and Agriculture</li>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_1sl0otraakld"></a>Procedural Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_brp7s9y1vj30"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p>ThreeAM, 3AM</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_vxy25uctv5gy"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Procedural Scorpius is a ransomware group discovered in September 2023, when researchers noticed Procedural Scorpius’ malware being deployed in a failed LockBit attack. This group distributes 3 am ransomware, and is thought to be linked to two other notorious ransomware groups, Conti and Ignoble Scorpius (distributor of Royal ransomware).</p>
<p>Procedural Scorpius escalates their extortion tactics by contacting their victim's social media followers, informing them of the data leak. They also use bots that post on highly visible X accounts to advertise the leaks. Procedural Scorpius targets medium to large companies in countries not within the Commonwealth of Independent States (CIS).</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_e5z2sp9pfkn6"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Procedural Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Agriculture</li>
<li>Financial Services</li>
<li>Manufacturing</li>
<li>Professional and Legal Services</li>
<li>Wholesale and Retail</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-135181-_h9k503rio7l4"></a>Protesting Scorpius</h3>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_hl7jzlpe6qze"></a>Also Known As</h4>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Cactus, Cactus Ransomware Group</span></p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_umdusgbrwd9m"></a>Summary</h4>
<p>Protesting Scorpius emerged as a ransomware threat actor in March 2023, employing double-extortion tactics. The group distinguishes itself through innovative tactics, often securing initial access to target networks by exploiting vulnerabilities in internet-facing software and services, such as virtual private network (VPN) appliances. This includes the use of zero-day vulnerabilities. The group also gains access through phishing attacks or by acquiring credentials via partnerships with malware distributors.</p>
<p>Protesting Scorpius targets are located primarily in the U.S. The group focuses on infiltrating networks of both public sector organizations and large commercial entities.</p>
<p>The group exfiltrates sensitive data from its victims and engages in extortion using peer-to-peer messaging services. Protesting Scorpius also uploads exfiltrated files to its own leak site to apply additional pressure to victims.</p>
<h4><a id="post-135181-_36z2y22byekm"></a>Sectors Impacted</h4>
<p>Protesting Scorpius has previously impacted organizations in the following sectors:</p>

<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Aerospace and Defense</span></li>

<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Financial Services</span></li>
